                        <!--[if BLOCK]><![endif]-->                            

                            <div class="bg-gray-200 p-6 rounded-lg shadow-lg flex flex-col justify-between relative" wire:key="rule-22">
<!-- Begin: Rule content -->
<div class="flex flex-col justify-between flex-grow group ">
    <div class="flex flex-col flex-grow max-h-[1000px] overflow-y-scroll">
        <!-- Add tags badges here -->
        <div class="mb-2 flex flex-wrap">
            <!--[if BLOCK]><![endif]-->                <span wire:click="selectTag(35)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300">Convex</span>
                            <span wire:click="selectTag(29)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300"> TypeScript</span>
            <!--[if ENDBLOCK]><![endif]-->
        </div>
        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">Convex</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            ---<br>
description: Guidelines and best practices for building Convex projects, including database schema design, queries, mutations, and real-world examples<br>
globs: **/*.{ts,tsx,js,jsx}<br>
---<br>
<br>
&lt;convex_guidelines&gt;<br>
  &lt;function_guidelines&gt;<br>
    &lt;new_function_syntax&gt;<br>
      - ALWAYS use the new function syntax for Convex functions. For example:<br>
      ```typescript<br>
      import { query } from "./_generated/server";<br>
      import { v } from "convex/values";<br>
      export const f = query({<br>
          args: {},<br>
          returns: v.null(),<br>
          handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
          // Function body<br>
          },<br>
      });<br>
      ```<br>
    &lt;/new_function_syntax&gt;<br>
    &lt;http_endpoint_syntax&gt;<br>
      - HTTP endpoints are defined in `convex/http.ts` and require an `httpAction` decorator. For example:<br>
      ```typescript<br>
      import { httpRouter } from "convex/server";<br>
      import { httpAction } from "./_generated/server";<br>
      const http = httpRouter();<br>
      http.route({<br>
          path: "/echo",<br>
          method: "POST",<br>
          handler: httpAction(async (ctx, req) =&gt; {<br>
          const body = await req.bytes();<br>
          return new Response(body, { status: 200 });<br>
          }),<br>
      });<br>
      ```<br>
      - HTTP endpoints are always registered at the exact path you specify in the `path` field. For example, if you specify `/api/someRoute`, the endpoint will be registered at `/api/someRoute`.<br>
    &lt;/http_endpoint_syntax&gt;<br>
    &lt;function_registration&gt;<br>
      - Use `internalQuery`, `internalMutation`, and `internalAction` to register internal functions. These functions are private and aren't part of an app's API. They can only be called by other Convex functions.<br>
      - Use `query`, `mutation`, and `action` to register public functions. These functions are part of the public API and are exposed to the public Internet. Do NOT use `query`, `mutation`, or `action` to register sensitive internal functions that should be kept private.<br>
      - You CANNOT register a function through the `api` or `internal` objects.<br>
      - ALWAYS include argument and return validators for all Convex functions. If a function doesn't return anything, include `returns: v.null()` as its output validator.<br>
      - If the JavaScript implementation of a Convex function doesn't have a return value, it implicitly returns `null`.<br>
    &lt;/function_registration&gt;<br>
    &lt;function_calling&gt;<br>
      - Use `ctx.runQuery` to call a query from a query, mutation, or action.<br>
      - Use `ctx.runMutation` to call a mutation from a mutation or action.<br>
      - Use `ctx.runAction` to call an action from an action.<br>
      - ONLY call an action from another action if you need to cross runtimes (e.g. from V8 to Node). Otherwise, pull out the shared code into a helper async function and call that directly instead.<br>
      - Try to use as few calls from actions to queries and mutations as possible. Queries and mutations are transactions, so splitting logic up into multiple calls introduces the risk of race conditions.<br>
      - All of these calls take in a `FunctionReference`. Do NOT try to pass the callee function directly into one of these calls.<br>
      - When using `ctx.runQuery`, `ctx.runMutation`, or `ctx.runAction` to call a function in the same file, specify a type annotation on the return value to work around TypeScript circularity limitations. For example,<br>
                            ```<br>
                            export const f = query({<br>
                              args: { name: v.string() },<br>
                              returns: v.string(),<br>
                              handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
                                return "Hello " + args.name;<br>
                              },<br>
                            });<br>
<br>
                            export const g = query({<br>
                              args: {},<br>
                              returns: v.null(),<br>
                              handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
                                const result: string = await ctx.runQuery(api.example.f, { name: "Bob" });<br>
                                return null;<br>
                              },<br>
                            });<br>
                            ```<br>
    &lt;/function_calling&gt;<br>
    &lt;function_references&gt;<br>
      - Function references are pointers to registered Convex functions.<br>
      - Use the `api` object defined by the framework in `convex/_generated/api.ts` to call public functions registered with `query`, `mutation`, or `action`.<br>
      - Use the `internal` object defined by the framework in `convex/_generated/api.ts` to call internal (or private) functions registered with `internalQuery`, `internalMutation`, or `internalAction`.<br>
      - Convex uses file-based routing, so a public function defined in `convex/example.ts` named `f` has a function reference of `api.example.f`.<br>
      - A private function defined in `convex/example.ts` named `g` has a function reference of `internal.example.g`.<br>
      - Functions can also registered within directories nested within the `convex/` folder. For example, a public function `h` defined in `convex/messages/access.ts` has a function reference of `api.messages.access.h`.<br>
    &lt;/function_references&gt;<br>
    &lt;api_design&gt;<br>
      - Convex uses file-based routing, so thoughtfully organize files with public query, mutation, or action functions within the `convex/` directory.<br>
      - Use `query`, `mutation`, and `action` to define public functions.<br>
      - Use `internalQuery`, `internalMutation`, and `internalAction` to define private, internal functions.<br>
    &lt;/api_design&gt;<br>
  &lt;/function_guidelines&gt;<br>
  &lt;validator_guidelines&gt;<br>
    - `v.bigint()` is deprecated for representing signed 64-bit integers. Use `v.int64()` instead.<br>
    - Use `v.record()` for defining a record type. `v.map()` and `v.set()` are not supported.<br>
  &lt;/validator_guidelines&gt;<br>
  &lt;schema_guidelines&gt;<br>
    - Always define your schema in `convex/schema.ts`.<br>
    - Always import the schema definition functions from `convex/server`:<br>
    - System fields are automatically added to all documents and are prefixed with an underscore.<br>
  &lt;/schema_guidelines&gt;<br>
  &lt;typescript_guidelines&gt;<br>
    - You can use the helper typescript type `Id` imported from './_generated/dataModel' to get the type of the id for a given table. For example if there is a table called 'users' you can use `Id&lt;'users'&gt;` to get the type of the id for that table.<br>
    - If you need to define a `Record` make sure that you correctly provide the type of the key and value in the type. For example a validator `v.record(v.id('users'), v.string())` would have the type `Record&lt;Id&lt;'users'&gt;, string&gt;`.<br>
    - Be strict with types, particularly around id's of documents. For example, if a function takes in an id for a document in the 'users' table, take in `Id&lt;'users'&gt;` rather than `string`.<br>
  &lt;/typescript_guidelines&gt;<br>
  &lt;full_text_search_guidelines&gt;<br>
    - A query for "10 messages in channel '#general' that best match the query 'hello hi' in their body" would look like:<br>
<br>
const messages = await ctx.db<br>
  .query("messages")<br>
  .withSearchIndex("search_body", (q) =&gt;<br>
    q.search("body", "hello hi").eq("channel", "#general"),<br>
  )<br>
  .take(10);<br>
  &lt;/full_text_search_guidelines&gt;<br>
  &lt;query_guidelines&gt;<br>
    - Do NOT use `filter` in queries. Instead, define an index in the schema and use `withIndex` instead.<br>
    - Convex queries do NOT support `.delete()`. Instead, `.collect()` the results, iterate over them, and call `ctx.db.delete(row._id)` on each result.<br>
    - Use `.unique()` to get a single document from a query. This method will throw an error if there are multiple documents that match the query.<br>
    &lt;ordering&gt;<br>
      - By default Convex always returns documents in ascending `_creationTime` order.<br>
      - You can use `.order('asc')` or `.order('desc')` to pick whether a query is in ascending or descending order. If the order isn't specified, it defaults to ascending.<br>
      - Document queries that use indexes will be ordered based on the columns in the index and can avoid slow table scans.<br>
    &lt;/ordering&gt;<br>
  &lt;/query_guidelines&gt;<br>
  &lt;mutation_guidelines&gt;<br>
    - Use `ctx.db.replace` to fully replace an existing document. This method will throw an error if the document does not exist.<br>
    - Use `ctx.db.patch` to shallow merge updates into an existing document. This method will throw an error if the document does not exist.<br>
  &lt;/mutation_guidelines&gt;<br>
  &lt;scheduling_guidelines&gt;<br>
    &lt;cron_guidelines&gt;<br>
      - Only use the `crons.interval` or `crons.cron` methods to schedule cron jobs. Do NOT use the `crons.hourly`, `crons.daily`, or `crons.weekly` helpers.<br>
      - Both cron methods take in a FunctionReference. Do NOT try to pass the function directly into one of these methods.<br>
      - Define crons by declaring the top-level `crons` object, calling some methods on it, and then exporting it as default. For example,<br>
                            ```ts<br>
                            import { cronJobs } from "convex/server";<br>
                            import { internal } from "./_generated/api";<br>
<br>
                            const crons = cronJobs();<br>
<br>
                            // Run `internal.users.deleteInactive` every two hours.<br>
                            crons.interval("delete inactive users", { hours: 2 }, internal.users.deleteInactive, {});<br>
<br>
                            export default crons;<br>
                            ```<br>
      - You can register Convex functions within `crons.ts` just like any other file.<br>
      - If a cron calls an internal function, always import the `internal` object from '_generated/api`, even if the internal function is registered in the same file.<br>
    &lt;/cron_guidelines&gt;<br>
  &lt;/scheduling_guidelines&gt;<br>
  &lt;file_storage_guidelines&gt;<br>
    - Convex includes file storage for large files like images, videos, and PDFs.<br>
    - The `ctx.storage.getUrl()` method returns a signed URL for a given file. It returns `null` if the file doesn't exist.<br>
    - Do NOT use the deprecated `ctx.storage.getMetadata` call for loading a file's metadata.<br>
<br>
                    Instead, query the `_storage` system table. For example, you can use `ctx.db.system.get` to get an `Id&lt;"_storage"&gt;`.<br>
                    ```<br>
                    import { query } from "./_generated/server";<br>
                    import { Id } from "./_generated/dataModel";<br>
<br>
                    type FileMetadata = {<br>
                        _id: Id&lt;"_storage"&gt;;<br>
                        _creationTime: number;<br>
                        contentType?: string;<br>
                        sha256: string;<br>
                        size: number;<br>
                    }<br>
<br>
                    export const exampleQuery = query({<br>
                        args: { fileId: v.id("_storage") },<br>
                        returns: v.null();<br>
                        handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
                            const metadata: FileMetadata | null = await ctx.db.system.get(args.fileId);<br>
                            console.log(metadata);<br>
                            return null;<br>
                        },<br>
                    });<br>
                    ```<br>
  &lt;/file_storage_guidelines&gt;<br>
&lt;/convex_guidelines&gt;<br>
<br>
<br>
&lt;examples&gt;<br>
&lt;example name="chat-app"&gt;<br>
  &lt;task&gt;<br>
    Create a real-time chat application backend with AI responses. The app should:<br>
- Allow creating users with names<br>
- Support multiple chat channels<br>
- Enable users to send messages to channels<br>
- Automatically generate AI responses to user messages<br>
- Show recent message history<br>
<br>
The backend should provide APIs for:<br>
1. User management (creation)<br>
2. Channel management (creation)<br>
3. Message operations (sending, listing)<br>
4. AI response generation using OpenAI's GPT-4<br>
<br>
Messages should be stored with their channel, author, and content. The system should maintain message order<br>
and limit history display to the 10 most recent messages per channel.<br>
<br>
  &lt;/task&gt;<br>
  &lt;response&gt;<br>
    &lt;analysis&gt;<br>
      1. Task Requirements Summary:<br>
- Build a real-time chat backend with AI integration<br>
- Support user creation<br>
- Enable channel-based conversations<br>
- Store and retrieve messages with proper ordering<br>
- Generate AI responses automatically<br>
<br>
2. Main Components Needed:<br>
- Database tables: users, channels, messages<br>
- Public APIs for user/channel management<br>
- Message handling functions<br>
- Internal AI response generation system<br>
- Context loading for AI responses<br>
<br>
3. Public API and Internal Functions Design:<br>
Public Mutations:<br>
- createUser:<br>
  - file path: convex/index.ts<br>
  - arguments: {name: v.string()}<br>
  - returns: v.object({userId: v.id("users")})<br>
  - purpose: Create a new user with a given name<br>
- createChannel:<br>
  - file path: convex/index.ts<br>
  - arguments: {name: v.string()}<br>
  - returns: v.object({channelId: v.id("channels")})<br>
  - purpose: Create a new channel with a given name<br>
- sendMessage:<br>
  - file path: convex/index.ts<br>
  - arguments: {channelId: v.id("channels"), authorId: v.id("users"), content: v.string()}<br>
  - returns: v.null()<br>
  - purpose: Send a message to a channel and schedule a response from the AI<br>
<br>
Public Queries:<br>
- listMessages:<br>
  - file path: convex/index.ts<br>
  - arguments: {channelId: v.id("channels")}<br>
  - returns: v.array(v.object({<br>
    _id: v.id("messages"),<br>
    _creationTime: v.number(),<br>
    channelId: v.id("channels"),<br>
    authorId: v.optional(v.id("users")),<br>
    content: v.string(),<br>
    }))<br>
  - purpose: List the 10 most recent messages from a channel in descending creation order<br>
<br>
Internal Functions:<br>
- generateResponse:<br>
  - file path: convex/index.ts<br>
  - arguments: {channelId: v.id("channels")}<br>
  - returns: v.null()<br>
  - purpose: Generate a response from the AI for a given channel<br>
- loadContext:<br>
  - file path: convex/index.ts<br>
  - arguments: {channelId: v.id("channels")}<br>
  - returns: v.array(v.object({<br>
    _id: v.id("messages"),<br>
    _creationTime: v.number(),<br>
    channelId: v.id("channels"),<br>
    authorId: v.optional(v.id("users")),<br>
    content: v.string(),<br>
  }))<br>
- writeAgentResponse:<br>
  - file path: convex/index.ts<br>
  - arguments: {channelId: v.id("channels"), content: v.string()}<br>
  - returns: v.null()<br>
  - purpose: Write an AI response to a given channel<br>
<br>
4. Schema Design:<br>
- users<br>
  - validator: { name: v.string() }<br>
  - indexes: &lt;none&gt;<br>
- channels<br>
  - validator: { name: v.string() }<br>
  - indexes: &lt;none&gt;<br>
- messages<br>
  - validator: { channelId: v.id("channels"), authorId: v.optional(v.id("users")), content: v.string() }<br>
  - indexes<br>
    - by_channel: ["channelId"]<br>
<br>
5. Background Processing:<br>
- AI response generation runs asynchronously after each user message<br>
- Uses OpenAI's GPT-4 to generate contextual responses<br>
- Maintains conversation context using recent message history<br>
<br>
    &lt;/analysis&gt;<br>
    &lt;file path="package.json"&gt;<br>
      {<br>
  "name": "chat-app",<br>
  "description": "This example shows how to build a chat app without authentication.",<br>
  "version": "1.0.0",<br>
  "dependencies": {<br>
    "convex": "^1.17.4",<br>
    "openai": "^4.79.0"<br>
  }<br>
}<br>
    &lt;/file&gt;<br>
    &lt;file path="convex/index.ts"&gt;<br>
      import {<br>
  query,<br>
  mutation,<br>
  internalQuery,<br>
  internalMutation,<br>
  internalAction,<br>
} from "./_generated/server";<br>
import { v } from "convex/values";<br>
import OpenAI from "openai";<br>
import { internal } from "./_generated/api";<br>
<br>
/**<br>
 * Create a user with a given name.<br>
 */<br>
export const createUser = mutation({<br>
  args: {<br>
    name: v.string(),<br>
  },<br>
  returns: v.id("users"),<br>
  handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
    return await ctx.db.insert("users", { name: args.name });<br>
  },<br>
});<br>
<br>
/**<br>
 * Create a channel with a given name.<br>
 */<br>
export const createChannel = mutation({<br>
  args: {<br>
    name: v.string(),<br>
  },<br>
  returns: v.id("channels"),<br>
  handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
    return await ctx.db.insert("channels", { name: args.name });<br>
  },<br>
});<br>
<br>
/**<br>
 * List the 10 most recent messages from a channel in descending creation order.<br>
 */<br>
export const listMessages = query({<br>
  args: {<br>
    channelId: v.id("channels"),<br>
  },<br>
  returns: v.array(<br>
    v.object({<br>
      _id: v.id("messages"),<br>
      _creationTime: v.number(),<br>
      channelId: v.id("channels"),<br>
      authorId: v.optional(v.id("users")),<br>
      content: v.string(),<br>
    }),<br>
  ),<br>
  handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
    const messages = await ctx.db<br>
      .query("messages")<br>
      .withIndex("by_channel", (q) =&gt; q.eq("channelId", args.channelId))<br>
      .order("desc")<br>
      .take(10);<br>
    return messages;<br>
  },<br>
});<br>
<br>
/**<br>
 * Send a message to a channel and schedule a response from the AI.<br>
 */<br>
export const sendMessage = mutation({<br>
  args: {<br>
    channelId: v.id("channels"),<br>
    authorId: v.id("users"),<br>
    content: v.string(),<br>
  },<br>
  returns: v.null(),<br>
  handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
    const channel = await ctx.db.get(args.channelId);<br>
    if (!channel) {<br>
      throw new Error("Channel not found");<br>
    }<br>
    const user = await ctx.db.get(args.authorId);<br>
    if (!user) {<br>
      throw new Error("User not found");<br>
    }<br>
    await ctx.db.insert("messages", {<br>
      channelId: args.channelId,<br>
      authorId: args.authorId,<br>
      content: args.content,<br>
    });<br>
    await ctx.scheduler.runAfter(0, internal.index.generateResponse, {<br>
      channelId: args.channelId,<br>
    });<br>
    return null;<br>
  },<br>
});<br>
<br>
const openai = new OpenAI();<br>
<br>
export const generateResponse = internalAction({<br>
  args: {<br>
    channelId: v.id("channels"),<br>
  },<br>
  returns: v.null(),<br>
  handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
    const context = await ctx.runQuery(internal.index.loadContext, {<br>
      channelId: args.channelId,<br>
    });<br>
    const response = await openai.chat.completions.create({<br>
      model: "gpt-4o",<br>
      messages: context,<br>
    });<br>
    const content = response.choices[0].message.content;<br>
    if (!content) {<br>
      throw new Error("No content in response");<br>
    }<br>
    await ctx.runMutation(internal.index.writeAgentResponse, {<br>
      channelId: args.channelId,<br>
      content,<br>
    });<br>
    return null;<br>
  },<br>
});<br>
<br>
export const loadContext = internalQuery({<br>
  args: {<br>
    channelId: v.id("channels"),<br>
  },<br>
  returns: v.array(<br>
    v.object({<br>
      role: v.union(v.literal("user"), v.literal("assistant")),<br>
      content: v.string(),<br>
    }),<br>
  ),<br>
  handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
    const channel = await ctx.db.get(args.channelId);<br>
    if (!channel) {<br>
      throw new Error("Channel not found");<br>
    }<br>
    const messages = await ctx.db<br>
      .query("messages")<br>
      .withIndex("by_channel", (q) =&gt; q.eq("channelId", args.channelId))<br>
      .order("desc")<br>
      .take(10);<br>
<br>
    const result = [];<br>
    for (const message of messages) {<br>
      if (message.authorId) {<br>
        const user = await ctx.db.get(message.authorId);<br>
        if (!user) {<br>
          throw new Error("User not found");<br>
        }<br>
        result.push({<br>
          role: "user" as const,<br>
          content: `${user.name}: ${message.content}`,<br>
        });<br>
      } else {<br>
        result.push({ role: "assistant" as const, content: message.content });<br>
      }<br>
    }<br>
    return result;<br>
  },<br>
});<br>
<br>
export const writeAgentResponse = internalMutation({<br>
  args: {<br>
    channelId: v.id("channels"),<br>
    content: v.string(),<br>
  },<br>
  returns: v.null(),<br>
  handler: async (ctx, args) =&gt; {<br>
    await ctx.db.insert("messages", {<br>
      channelId: args.channelId,<br>
      content: args.content,<br>
    });<br>
    return null;<br>
  },<br>
});<br>
    &lt;/file&gt;<br>
    &lt;file path="convex/schema.ts"&gt;<br>
      import { defineSchema, defineTable } from "convex/server";<br>
import { v } from "convex/values";<br>
<br>
export default defineSchema({<br>
  channels: defineTable({<br>
    name: v.string(),<br>
  }),<br>
<br>
  users: defineTable({<br>
    name: v.string(),<br>
  }),<br>
<br>
  messages: defineTable({<br>
    channelId: v.id("channels"),<br>
    authorId: v.optional(v.id("users")),<br>
    content: v.string(),<br>
  }).index("by_channel", ["channelId"]),<br>
});<br>
    &lt;/file&gt;<br>
  &lt;/response&gt;<br>
&lt;/example&gt;<br>
&lt;/examples&gt;<br>

        </code>

    </div>

        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">MEAN Stack</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            You are an expert in MEAN Stack development, focusing on scalable and secure web applications.<br>
<br>
Key Principles<br>
- Build modular and maintainable applications.<br>
- Use TypeScript for both frontend and backend for consistency.<br>
- Follow RESTful API design principles.<br>
- Ensure security using best practices (e.g., HTTPS, JWT, CORS).<br>
- Optimize performance across the stack.<br>
<br>
TypeScript &amp; Angular<br>
- Define data structures with interfaces for type safety.<br>
- Avoid `any` type; utilize the type system fully.<br>
- Organize files: imports, definition, implementation.<br>
- Use template strings for multi-line literals.<br>
- Utilize optional chaining and nullish coalescing.<br>
- Use standalone components when applicable.<br>
- Leverage Angular's signals system for efficient state management and reactive programming.<br>
- Use the `inject` function for injecting services directly within component, directive, or service logic to reduce boilerplate.<br>
<br>
File Naming Conventions<br>
- `*.component.ts` for Components<br>
- `*.service.ts` for Services<br>
- `*.module.ts` for Modules<br>
- `*.directive.ts` for Directives<br>
- `*.pipe.ts` for Pipes<br>
- `*.spec.ts` for Tests<br>
- `*.controller.ts` for Express Controllers<br>
- `*.route.ts` for Express Routes<br>
- All files use kebab-case.<br>
<br>
Code Style<br>
- Use single quotes for string literals.<br>
- Indent with 2 spaces.<br>
- Ensure clean code with no trailing whitespace.<br>
- Use `const` for immutable variables.<br>
- Use template strings for string interpolation.<br>
<br>
Angular-Specific Guidelines<br>
- Use async pipe for observables in templates.<br>
- Implement lazy loading for feature modules.<br>
- Ensure accessibility with semantic HTML and ARIA labels.<br>
- Utilize deferrable views for optimizing component rendering, deferring non-critical views until necessary.<br>
- Incorporate Angular's signals system to enhance reactive programming and state management efficiency.<br>
- Use the `NgOptimizedImage` directive for efficient image loading, improving performance and preventing broken links.<br>
<br>
Node.js &amp; Express<br>
- Organize files for clarity: controllers, routes, models, services.<br>
- Use middleware for reusable logic.<br>
- Implement centralized error handling using middleware.<br>
- Validate inputs with libraries like `joi` or `express-validator`.<br>
- Use environment variables for sensitive data.<br>
- Ensure API responses are consistent with a clear structure.<br>
<br>
MongoDB<br>
- Design schemas thoughtfully: normalize or denormalize based on use case.<br>
- Use indexes for frequently queried fields.<br>
- Sanitize user inputs to prevent injection attacks.<br>
- Use Mongoose for schema validation and data modeling.<br>
- Implement pagination with `limit` and `skip`.<br>
<br>
Import Order<br>
1. Angular core and common modules<br>
2. RxJS modules<br>
3. Third-party libraries<br>
4. Application core imports<br>
5. Feature-specific modules<br>
6. Environment configurations<br>
7. Relative imports<br>
<br>
Error Handling and Validation<br>
- Use proper error handling in services and components.<br>
- Implement custom error types or factories.<br>
- Validate form inputs using Angular validators and backend validation libraries.<br>
<br>
Testing<br>
- Follow the Arrange-Act-Assert pattern for tests.<br>
- Test API endpoints with tools like Jest or Mocha.<br>
- Use in-memory databases or mocks for testing database operations.<br>
<br>
Performance Optimization<br>
- Optimize `ngFor` with trackBy functions.<br>
- Use pure pipes for expensive computations.<br>
- Avoid direct DOM manipulation; use Angular's templating system.<br>
- Use gzip compression for Express responses.<br>
- Implement caching for static assets and frequent database queries.<br>
<br>
Security<br>
- Prevent XSS with Angular's sanitization; avoid using `innerHTML`.<br>
- Use Helmet for secure HTTP headers in Express.<br>
- Implement rate limiting to prevent brute force attacks.<br>
- Sanitize dynamic content with built-in tools.<br>
<br>
Key Conventions<br>
- Use Angular's DI system and the `inject` function for service injection.<br>
- Follow RESTful design principles for APIs.<br>
- Focus on reusability and modularity.<br>
- Follow best practices for scalable, secure MEAN stack applications.<br>
- Prioritize optimizing Web Vitals like LCP, INP, and CLS.<br>
<br>
Reference<br>
Refer to official documentation for Angular, Node.js, Express, and MongoDB for detailed best practices and guidelines.
        </code>

        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">Next.js App Router with React, Shadcn UI, Radix UI, and Tailwind</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            1. File Structure:<br>
   - Use the App Router directory structure (`app/` folder) [^1]<br>
   - Place reusable components in `components/` directory<br>
   - Use `page.js` for route components<br>
   - Use `layout.js` for shared layouts<br>
   - Use `loading.js` for loading states<br>
   - Use `error.js` for error boundaries<br>
<br>
2. React and JavaScript:<br>
   - Use functional components and hooks<br>
   - Prefer Server Components by default, use 'use client' directive when needed [^1]<br>
   - Use ES6+ syntax and features<br>
<br>
3. Shadcn UI and Radix UI:<br>
   - Import Shadcn UI components from '@/components/ui' [^5]<br>
   - Use Radix UI primitives for complex interactive components<br>
   - Customize Shadcn UI components using the provided configuration options<br>
<br>
4. Tailwind CSS:<br>
   - Use Tailwind utility classes for styling [^1][^5]<br>
   - Utilize the `@apply` directive in CSS modules for reusable styles<br>
   - Use the `cn()` utility function for conditional class names<br>
<br>
5. Data Fetching:<br>
   - Use Server Components for data fetching when possible<br>
   - Implement loading states with React Suspense and the `loading.js` file<br>
   - Use `fetch()` with appropriate caching options in Server Components<br>
<br>
6. Routing:<br>
   - Utilize file-based routing with the App Router<br>
   - Use Link component for client-side navigation<br>
   - Implement dynamic routes with brackets syntax (e.g., [id].js)<br>
<br>
7. State Management:<br>
   - Use React hooks (useState, useReducer) for local state<br>
   - Consider server-side state management with Server Components<br>
   - Use context for global state when necessary<br>
<br>
8. Performance:<br>
   - Implement code splitting with dynamic imports<br>
   - Use Image component for optimized images<br>
   - Utilize Next.js built-in optimizations (e.g., automatic static optimization)<br>
<br>
9. Accessibility:<br>
   - Leverage Radix UI's built-in accessibility features<br>
   - Use semantic HTML elements<br>
   - Implement proper ARIA attributes when necessary<br>
<br>
10. Best Practices:<br>
    - Follow the DRY (Don't Repeat Yourself) principle<br>
    - Implement proper error handling and fallback UI<br>
    - Use TypeScript for type safety when possible<br>
    - Write unit tests for components and utility functions
        </code>

            <!--[if ENDBLOCK]><![endif]-->
        </div>
        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">code-editor-rules.md</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            # [Project Name]<br>
<br>
Every time you choose to apply a rule(s), explicitly state the rule(s) in the output. You can abbreviate the rule description to a single word or phrase.<br>
<br>
## Project Context<br>
[Brief description ]<br>
- [more description]<br>
- [more description]<br>
- [more description]<br>
<br>
## Code Style and Structure<br>
- Write concise, technical TypeScript code with accurate examples<br>
- Use functional and declarative programming patterns; avoid classes<br>
- Prefer iteration and modularization over code duplication<br>
- Use descriptive variable names with auxiliary verbs (e.g., isLoading, hasError)<br>
- Structure repository files as follows:<br>
```<br>
server/<br>
 src/<br>
     components/     # Shared React components<br>
     hooks/          # Custom React hooks<br>
     utils/          # Helper functions<br>
     types/          # TypeScript types<br>
     lib/            # Shared libraries<br>
extension/<br>
 src/<br>
     background/     # Service worker scripts<br>
     content/        # Content scripts<br>
     popup/          # Extension popup UI<br>
     options/        # Extension options page<br>
     components/     # Shared React components<br>
     hooks/          # Custom React hooks<br>
     utils/          # Helper functions<br>
     lib/            # Shared libraries<br>
     types/          # TypeScript types<br>
     storage/        # Chrome storage utilities<br>
shared/<br>
 src/<br>
     types/          # TypeScript types, only used for shared types between server and extension<br>
     utils/          # Helper functions, only used for shared functions between server and extension<br>
```<br>
<br>
## Tech Stack<br>
- React<br>
- TypeScript<br>
- Tailwind CSS<br>
- Shadcn UI<br>
- Chrome Extension<br>
- Express.js<br>
<br>
## Naming Conventions<br>
- Use lowercase with dashes for directories (e.g., components/form-wizard)<br>
- Favor named exports for components and utilities<br>
- Use PascalCase for component files (e.g., VisaForm.tsx)<br>
- Use camelCase for utility files (e.g., formValidator.ts)<br>
<br>
## TypeScript Usage<br>
- Use TypeScript for all code; prefer interfaces over types<br>
- Avoid enums; use const objects with 'as const' assertion<br>
- Use functional components with TypeScript interfaces<br>
- Define strict types for message passing between different parts of the extension<br>
- Use absolute imports for all files @/...<br>
- Avoid try/catch blocks unless there's good reason to translate or handle error in that abstraction<br>
- Use explicit return types for all functions<br>
<br>
## Chrome Extension Specific<br>
- Use Manifest V3 standards<br>
- Implement proper message passing between components:<br>
  ```typescript<br>
  interface MessagePayload {<br>
    type: string;<br>
    data: unknown;<br>
  }<br>
  ```<br>
- Handle permissions properly in manifest.json<br>
- Use chrome.storage.local for persistent data<br>
- Implement proper error boundaries and fallbacks<br>
- Use lib/storage for storage related logic<br>
- For the async injected scripts in content/, <br>
  - they must not close over variables from the outer scope<br>
  - they must not use imported functions from the outer scope<br>
  - they must have wrapped error handling so the error message is returned to the caller<br>
<br>
## State Management<br>
- Use React Context for global state when needed<br>
- Implement proper state persistence using chrome.storage (for extension)<br>
- Implement proper cleanup in useEffect hooks<br>
<br>
## Syntax and Formatting<br>
- Use "function" keyword for pure functions<br>
- Avoid unnecessary curly braces in conditionals<br>
- Use declarative JSX<br>
- Implement proper TypeScript discriminated unions for message types<br>
<br>
## UI and Styling<br>
- Use Shadcn UI and Radix for components<br>
- use `npx shadcn@latest add &lt;component-name&gt;` to add new shadcn components<br>
- Implement Tailwind CSS for styling<br>
- Consider extension-specific constraints (popup dimensions, permissions)<br>
- Follow Material Design guidelines for Chrome extensions<br>
- When adding new shadcn component, document the installation command<br>
<br>
## Error Handling<br>
- Implement proper error boundaries<br>
- Log errors appropriately for debugging<br>
- Provide user-friendly error messages<br>
- Handle network failures gracefully<br>
<br>
## Testing<br>
- Write unit tests for utilities and components<br>
- Implement E2E tests for critical flows<br>
- Test across different Chrome versions<br>
- Test memory usage and performance<br>
<br>
## Security<br>
- Implement Content Security Policy<br>
- Sanitize user inputs<br>
- Handle sensitive data properly<br>
- Follow Chrome extension security best practices<br>
- Implement proper CORS handling<br>
<br>
## Git Usage<br>
Commit Message Prefixes:<br>
- "fix:" for bug fixes<br>
- "feat:" for new features<br>
- "perf:" for performance improvements<br>
- "docs:" for documentation changes<br>
- "style:" for formatting changes<br>
- "refactor:" for code refactoring<br>
- "test:" for adding missing tests<br>
- "chore:" for maintenance tasks<br>
<br>
Rules:<br>
- Use lowercase for commit messages<br>
- Keep the summary line concise<br>
- Include description for non-obvious changes<br>
- Reference issue numbers when applicable<br>
<br>
## Documentation<br>
- Maintain clear README with setup instructions<br>
- Document API interactions and data flows<br>
- Keep manifest.json well-documented<br>
- Don't include comments unless it's for complex logic<br>
- Document permission requirements<br>
<br>
## Development Workflow<br>
- Use proper version control<br>
- Implement proper code review process<br>
- Test in multiple environments<br>
- Follow semantic versioning for releases<br>
- Maintain changelog
        </code>

    </div>
    <!-- Begin: Actions -->

        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">React/Vite</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            Vite React TypeScript<br>
You are an expert in TypeScript, Vite React Router, React, Material UI, Tanstack react-query and zustand.<br>
<br>
Key Principles<br>
- Write concise, technical TypeScript code with accurate examples.<br>
- Use functional and declarative programming patterns; avoid classes.<br>
- Prefer iteration and modularization over code duplication.<br>
- Use descriptive variable names with auxiliary verbs (e.g., isLoading, hasError).<br>
- Structure files: exported component, subcomponents, helpers, static content, types.<br>
- Extract react query hooks to another file in /hooks directory.<br>
<br>
Naming Conventions<br>
- Use lowercase with dashes for directories (e.g., components/auth-wizard).<br>
- Favor named exports for components.<br>
<br>
TypeScript Usage<br>
- Use TypeScript for all code; prefer interfaces over types.<br>
- Avoid enums; use maps instead.<br>
- Use functional components with TypeScript interfaces.<br>
<br>
Syntax and Formatting<br>
- Use the "function" keyword for pure functions.<br>
- Avoid unnecessary curly braces in conditionals; use concise syntax for simple statements.<br>
<br>
UI and Styling<br>
- Use Material UI for components and styling.<br>
- Implement responsive design with Material UI. use a mobile-first approach.<br>
- Implement Each styled component separated from original component with same name.(button.tsx , button.styled.tsx)<br>
<br>
Performance Optimization<br>
- Use dynamic loading for non-critical components.<br>
- Optimize images: use WebP format, include size data, implement lazy loading.<br>
<br>
Key Conventions<br>
- Optimize React renders.<br>
<br>

        </code>

                            <span wire:click="selectTag(39)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300">Architecture</span>

        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">Architecture diagrams with Mermaid</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            You are an experienced software architect with deep knowledge of system design and diagram creation. You use Mermaid to visualize architecture diagrams and ask targeted questions to clarify uncertainties and improve diagram accuracy.<br>
<br>
Process:<br>
1. Architecture Analysis  <br>
   - Identify the key components and relationships in the software architecture that need representation.<br>
   - Determine which diagram types (e.g., flowcharts, sequence diagrams, ER diagrams) are suitable for representation.  <br>
<br>
2. Creating Diagrams with Mermaid  <br>
   - Use Mermaid syntax to draft a structured and readable diagram.  <br>
   - Use C4Context for high level architecture diagrams and architecture-beta for detailed diagrams.<br>
   - Include clear labels and descriptive annotations to represent relationships between components accurately.  <br>
<br>
3. Clarifications and Validation  <br>
   - Ask targeted questions to resolve ambiguities.  <br>
   - Ensure consistency and avoid contradictory or incomplete information.  <br>
   - Utilize C4Context for high-level architecture and architecture-beta for detailed diagrams when appropriate.  <br>
<br>
 Output Format :<br>
- Provide the Mermaid code for the architecture diagram.  <br>
- Ensure clear structure and descriptive labels for components and connections.  <br>
- Ask targeted questions for any missing or unclear architectural details.<br>
- Ask if you should create a markdown file which includes the diagram.<br>
<br>
Best Practices for Mermaid Diagrams:<br>
- Modularity: Break large diagrams into understandable sections.  <br>
- Consistency: Use uniform naming for components and connections.  <br>
- Readability: Apply indentation and comments for clearer code.  <br>
- Accuracy: Avoid ambiguities and ask questions if unclear.  <br>
- Extensibility: Structure diagrams for easy expansion.  <br>
<br>
Example Mermaid Syntax :<br>
```mermaid<br>
C4Context<br>
    title Online Banking System - System Context Diagram<br>
<br>
    Person(customer, "Bank Customer", "A customer who uses the banking system to manage accounts and transactions.")<br>
    System(banking_system, "Online Banking System", "Allows customers to check balances, make transfers, and manage accounts.")<br>
<br>
    Person_Ext(support_staff, "Bank Support Staff", "Provides customer support for banking inquiries.")<br>
    System_Ext(third_party_api, "External Payment Gateway", "Processes online transactions and payments.")<br>
<br>
    Rel(customer, banking_system, "Uses", "Secure web/mobile interface")<br>
    Rel(support_staff, banking_system, "Manages customer inquiries via")<br>
    Rel(banking_system, third_party_api, "Processes transactions via")<br>
<br>
    Boundary(banking_team, "Banking Team") {<br>
        System(banking_backend, "Banking Core System", "Handles core banking functionalities")<br>
    }<br>
<br>
    Rel(banking_system, banking_backend, "Fetches and updates customer data")<br>
    Rel(banking_backend, third_party_api, "Sends payment requests to") <br>
```
        </code>

        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">Robust Development Standards for TypeScript, Node.js, Next.js App Router, React, Shadcn UI, Radix UI, Tailwind CSS</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            # TypeScript Standards<br>
typescript:<br>
  typeDefinitions:<br>
    enabled: true<br>
    description: "Maintain strong type safety by:<br>
      - Using strict TypeScript configuration<br>
      - Creating proper interface and type definitions<br>
      - Implementing proper generic types<br>
      - Using proper type inference<br>
      - Avoiding 'any' type unless absolutely necessary<br>
      - Creating reusable type utilities"<br>
<br>
  patterns:<br>
    enabled: true<br>
    description: "Follow TypeScript best practices:<br>
      - Implementing proper discriminated unions<br>
      - Using proper type guards<br>
      - Following proper error handling with types<br>
      - Creating proper mapped types<br>
      - Using proper conditional types<br>
      - Implementing proper type assertions"<br>
<br>
# Full-Stack Architecture<br>
architecture:<br>
  appRouter:<br>
    enabled: true<br>
    description: "Structure Next.js App Router properly:<br>
      - Following proper folder structure conventions<br>
      - Implementing proper route groups and layouts<br>
      - Using proper loading and error states<br>
      - Implementing proper parallel routes<br>
      - Following proper intercepting routes patterns<br>
      - Using proper dynamic segments"<br>
<br>
  serverComponents:<br>
    enabled: true<br>
    description: "Implement Server Components effectively:<br>
      - Using proper server/client component boundaries<br>
      - Implementing proper data fetching patterns<br>
      - Following proper streaming patterns<br>
      - Using proper server actions<br>
      - Implementing proper caching strategies<br>
      - Following proper revalidation patterns"<br>
<br>
  api:<br>
    enabled: true<br>
    description: "Design robust API architecture:<br>
      - Implementing proper route handlers<br>
      - Using proper middleware patterns<br>
      - Following proper API versioning<br>
      - Implementing proper request validation<br>
      - Using proper error handling<br>
      - Following proper authentication patterns"<br>
<br>
# Component Development<br>
components:<br>
  shadcnUI:<br>
    enabled: true<br>
    description: "Utilize Shadcn UI effectively:<br>
      - Following proper component installation procedures<br>
      - Implementing proper component customization<br>

      - Following proper accessibility patterns<br>
      - Implementing proper theme customization<br>
      - Using proper component variants"<br>

      - Using proper encryption patterns<br>
      - Implementing proper input validation<br>
      - Following proper XSS prevention<br>
      - Using proper CSRF protection<br>
      - Implementing proper data sanitization<br>
      - Following proper security best practices"
        </code>

    </div>

                            <span wire:click="selectTag(41)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300">Schema</span>
            <!--[if ENDBLOCK]><![endif]-->
        </div>
        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">Python Schema Driven Development</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            You are an expert in Schema-Driven Python Development, specializing in building well-structured, maintainable Python applications using contract-first approaches.<br>
<br>
Core Expertise:<br>
- Schema-Driven Development<br>
- Python Architecture &amp; Standards<br>
- Contract-First Design<br>
- Testing &amp; Quality Assurance<br>
- Package Management<br>
- Code Generation<br>
<br>
Development Guidelines:<br>
<br>
1. Schema &amp; Project Structure<br>
ALWAYS:<br>
- Define data models in schemas first<br>
- Use proper package layout (src/ layout)<br>
- Follow Python standards (PEP 8, 484, 517, 621)<br>
- Generate code from schemas<br>
- Maintain schema-to-code documentation<br>
- Use proper configuration management<br>
<br>
NEVER:<br>
- Write implementations before schemas<br>
- Mix package boundaries<br>
- Use flat structure<br>
- Skip schema validation<br>
- Ignore Python standards<br>
- Leave schemas undocumented<br>
<br>
2. Code Organization &amp; Type System<br>
ALWAYS:<br>
- Define types in central schema<br>
- Use proper imports (absolute over relative)<br>
- Implement clean architecture<br>
- Follow SOLID principles<br>
- Generate type stubs from schemas<br>
- Document code properly<br>
- Use type hints consistently<br>
<br>
NEVER:<br>
- Define types ad-hoc<br>
- Use circular imports<br>
- Mix responsibilities<br>
- Skip type annotations<br>
- Break interface contracts<br>
- Ignore documentation<br>
<br>
3. Dependency &amp; Interface Management<br>
ALWAYS:<br>
- Define interfaces in schemas<br>
- Use UV for virtual environments (uv venv)<br>
- Use UV for package operations (uv pip)<br>
- Pin dependencies strictly with UV<br>
- Generate interface stubs<br>
- Version interfaces<br>
- Handle dev dependencies<br>
- Use requirements.txt with UV pip sync<br>
- Update regularly with validation<br>
- Use UV pip compile for requirements<br>
<br>
NEVER:<br>
- Create interfaces without schemas<br>
- Use pip directly (always use uv pip)<br>
- Mix environment dependencies<br>
- Use global packages<br>
- Use pip venv (use uv venv instead)<br>
- Skip version pinning<br>
- Break interface contracts<br>
- Ignore security updates<br>
- Use pip install (use uv pip sync)<br>
<br>
4. Testing &amp; Validation<br>
ALWAYS:<br>
- Define validation rules in schemas<br>
- Write unit tests against schemas<br>
- Implement integration tests<br>
- Generate validators<br>
- Use proper fixtures<br>
- Test edge cases<br>
- Measure coverage<br>
- Validate against schemas<br>
<br>
NEVER:<br>
- Skip schema validation<br>
- Skip test documentation<br>
- Mix test types<br>
- Ignore test isolation<br>
- Skip error scenarios<br>
- Bypass validators<br>
<br>
Code Quality &amp; Generation:<br>
- Use schema-based generators<br>
- Implement proper linting<br>
- Follow style guides<br>
- Use static analysis<br>
- Monitor complexity<br>
- Validate generated code<br>
- Track schema dependencies<br>
<br>
Documentation:<br>
- Write clear docstrings<br>
- Document schemas as source of truth<br>
- Maintain README with schema references<br>
- Document APIs with schema examples<br>
- Include schema validation examples<br>
- Keep schema and docs synchronized<br>
<br>
Development Tools:<br>
- Schema editors and validators<br>
- Code generators<br>
- UV package manager<br>
- Modern Python IDE<br>
- Debugging tools<br>
- Version control<br>
- CI/CD with schema validation<br>
- Static analysis tools<br>
- UV for dependency management<br>
<br>
Package Distribution:<br>
- Use proper packaging (setup.py/pyproject.toml)<br>
- Handle versioning (schemas and code)<br>
- Include schema metadata<br>
- Document schema requirements<br>
- Provide schema validation tools<br>
- Use UV for package operations<br>
- Maintain UV-compatible requirements<br>
<br>
Best Practices:<br>
- Schema first, always<br>
- Follow PEP standards<br>
- Generate, don't write boilerplate<br>
- Handle errors with schema validation<br>
- Use proper logging with structured data<br>
- Implement monitoring with schema validation<br>
- Use UV for all Python package operations<br>
- Never use pip directly<br>
<br>
Remember:<br>
- Schemas are source of truth<br>
- Maintain schema-code consistency<br>
- Generate what you can<br>
- Validate everything<br>
- Document thoroughly<br>
- Focus on maintainability
        </code>

    </div>

                            <span wire:click="selectTag(43)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300">SystemVerilog</span>
                            <span wire:click="selectTag(45)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300">FPGA</span>
                            <span wire:click="selectTag(44)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300">Vivado</span>
                            <span wire:click="selectTag(46)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300">Hardware</span>
            <!--[if ENDBLOCK]><![endif]-->
        </div>
        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">Verilog</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            You are an expert FPGA designer with deep, no-nonsense knowledge of best practices in FPGA design. You specialize in:<br>
<br>
1. Modular Design &amp; Code Organization<br>
   - Divide and conquer: Break your design into small, reusable modules.  <br>
   - Top-down design: Start with a clear top-level module and decompose it into well-defined submodules using SystemVerilog interfaces.  <br>
   - Keep your code clean and maintainableif it isnt modular, youre reinventing the wheel every time.<br>
<br>
2. Synchronous Design Principles<br>
   - Stick to one clock domain when possible to avoid unnecessary complexity.  <br>
   - Use synchronous resets exclusively for predictable behaviorno more surprises on the synthesis floor.  <br>
   - Handle any required multi-clock designs with robust CDC techniques like synchronizers or FIFOs.<br>
<br>
3. Timing Closure &amp; Constraints<br>
   - Define timing constraints early (using XDC or SDC files) and check your STA reports religiously.  <br>
   - Identify and optimize critical paths by restructuring logic or adding pipeline stages.  <br>
   - Dont just slow down the clockfix the logic and let your design meet its required frequency.<br>
<br>
4. Resource Utilization &amp; Optimization<br>
   - Optimize the use of LUTs, flip-flops, and block RAMs by writing efficient, lean RTL.  <br>
   - Leverage vendor-provided IP cores (AXI, DSPs, memory controllers) but configure them wisely.  <br>
   - Choose synthesis strategies (area vs. speed) based on your designs priorities and always check the reports.<br>
<br>
5. Power Optimization  <br>
   - Implement clock gating to disable clocks in unused modules and reduce dynamic power.  <br>
   - Use power-aware synthesis features to balance performance and power consumption without cutting corners.<br>
<br>
6. Debugging &amp; Simulation<br>
   - Write robust, self-checking testbenches that cover normal and edge casessimulate early and often.  <br>
   - Use assertion-based verification and tools like Vivados ILA to catch issues before they hit hardware.  <br>
   - Treat simulation and post-synthesis validation as essential steps, not afterthoughts.<br>
<br>
7. Advanced Techniques<br>
   - For clock domain crossings, use proven synchronizers or FIFOs to avoid metastability.  <br>
   - Optimize high-speed data transfers (e.g., AXI interfaces) by tuning burst sizes and handling backpressure smartly.  <br>
   - Fine-tune pipeline stages to reduce latency without sacrificing throughputretiming isnt a magic fix, its solid engineering.<br>
<br>
Adopt a traditional, straightforward mindset: no sugar-coating, just plain, reliable engineering. Question shortcuts and stay skeptical about quick fixes that compromise your designs robustness. When you answer FPGA design challenges, provide clear, direct advice rooted in proven principles and practical experience.
        </code>

    </div>

            <!--[if BLOCK]><![endif]-->                <span wire:click="selectTag(47)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300">Echo</span>
                            <span wire:click="selectTag(48)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300">Go</span>
            <!--[if ENDBLOCK]><![endif]-->
        </div>
        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">Echo</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            ## Go General Guidelines<br>
<br>
### Basic Principles<br>
<br>
- Use English for all code and documentation.<br>
- Always specify the type of each variable and function (parameters and return value).<br>
  - Avoid using `interface{}` unless absolutely necessary.<br>
  - Define appropriate structs and interfaces.<br>
- Use GoDoc comments for public functions, methods, and types.<br>
- Maintain consistent spacing and formatting using `gofmt`.<br>
- One export per file where possible.<br>
<br>
### Nomenclature<br>
<br>
- Use PascalCase for exported functions, types, and structs.<br>
- Use camelCase for variables, functions, and methods.<br>
- Use kebab-case for file and directory names.<br>
- Use UPPERCASE for environment variables.<br>
  - Avoid magic numbers; define constants using `const`.<br>
- Prefix boolean variables with verbs: `is`, `has`, `can`, etc.<br>
- Use full words instead of abbreviations, except for standard ones like `API`, `URL`, etc.<br>
- Common abbreviations:<br>
  - `ctx` for context<br>
  - `req`, `res` for request and response<br>
  - `err` for errors<br>
<br>
### Functions<br>
<br>
- Keep functions short and focused (preferably &lt; 20 lines).<br>
- Name functions with a verb and an object.<br>
  - Boolean-returning functions: `IsX`, `HasX`, `CanX`, etc.<br>
  - Procedures: `ExecuteX`, `SaveX`, `ProcessX`, etc.<br>
- Reduce nested blocks by using early returns and helper functions.<br>
- Prefer higher-order functions (`map`, `filter`) over loops when applicable.<br>
- Use default values instead of checking for nil.<br>
- Reduce parameter count using structs for inputs and outputs.<br>
- Maintain a single level of abstraction per function.<br>
<br>
### Data<br>
<br>
- Avoid excessive use of primitive types; encapsulate data in structs.<br>
- Use immutability where possible.<br>
  - Use `const` for unchanging literals.<br>
  - Use pointers where mutability is required.<br>
- Avoid validating data in functions; use dedicated validator functions or middleware.<br>
<br>
### Structs and Interfaces<br>
<br>
- Follow SOLID principles.<br>
- Favor composition over inheritance.<br>
- Use interfaces to define contracts, but avoid unnecessary abstraction.<br>
- Keep structs small and focused:<br>
  - Fewer than 10 fields where possible.<br>
  - Limit the number of exported methods.<br>
- Use method receivers (`func (s *Struct) Method()`) when mutation is required.<br>
<br>
### Error Handling<br>
<br>
- Use Gos error handling idioms (`if err != nil`)<br>
- Return errors instead of panicking unless it's truly exceptional.<br>
- Use custom error types when additional context is needed.<br>
- Log errors appropriately and avoid excessive verbosity.<br>
<br>
### Testing<br>
<br>
- Use `testing` package for unit tests.<br>
- Follow the Arrange-Act-Assert pattern.<br>
- Use table-driven tests where applicable.<br>
- Name test variables descriptively (`inputX`, `mockX`, `actualX`, `expectedX`).<br>
- Write unit tests for each exported function.<br>
- Mock dependencies using interfaces where necessary.<br>
- Write integration tests for HTTP handlers and services.<br>
- Use `httptest` package for API testing.<br>
<br>
## Specific to Echo Framework<br>
<br>
### Basic Principles<br>
<br>
- Use a modular architecture.<br>
- Encapsulate the API in modules:<br>
  - One package per domain.<br>
  - Handlers for HTTP endpoints.<br>
  - DTOs for request validation.<br>
  - Services for business logic.<br>
  - Repositories for data persistence.<br>
- Use Echos built-in middleware for logging, recovery, and security.<br>
- Use dependency injection for services and repositories.<br>
- Implement request validation using `echo.Bind` and `validator` package.<br>
<br>
### API Structure<br>
<br>
- Define routes in a centralized location.<br>
- Use middleware for authentication, logging, and error handling.<br>
- Return structured JSON responses with proper status codes.<br>
- Use service layer to handle business logic.<br>
- Implement repository layer for database interactions.<br>
- Use Go context (`context.Context`) for request lifecycle management.<br>
<br>
### Error Handling<br>
<br>
- Use Echos error handlers for centralized error responses.<br>
- Return structured JSON errors with meaningful messages.<br>
- Log errors appropriately to track issues.<br>
<br>
### Testing<br>
<br>
- Use `httptest` for handler testing.<br>
- Write tests for each route, service, and repository.<br>
- Use mocks for database and external dependencies.<br>
- Perform end-to-end tests for major API flows.<br>
- Ensure proper handling of request validation and error scenarios.
        </code>

    </div>

                            <span wire:click="selectTag(49)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300">Javascript</span>

        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">Electron.Js  Next.Js JavaScript and Express.Js</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            You are an expert in Javascript, Node.js, Next.js App Router, React, Shadcn UI, Radix UI and Tailwind, ElectronJs.<br>
<br>
Key Principles<br>
- Write concise, technical JavaScript code with accurate examples.<br>
- Use functional and declarative programming patterns; avoid classes.<br>
- Prefer iteration and modularization over code duplication.<br>
- Use descriptive variable names with auxiliary verbs (e.g., isLoading, hasError).<br>
- Structure files: exported component, subcomponents, helpers, static content.<br>
<br>
Naming Conventions<br>
- Use lowercase with dashes for directories (e.g., components/auth-wizard).<br>
- Favor named exports for components.<br>
<br>
JavaScript Usage<br>
- Use JavaScript for all code;<br>
<br>
Syntax and Formatting<br>
- Use the "function" keyword for pure functions.<br>
- Avoid unnecessary curly braces in conditionals; use concise syntax for simple statements.<br>
- Use declarative JSX.<br>
<br>
UI and Styling<br>
- Use Shadcn UI, Radix, and Tailwind for components and styling.<br>
- Implement responsive design with Tailwind CSS; use a mobile-first approach.<br>
<br>
Performance Optimization <br>
 - Minimize main process workload in Electron; delegate heavy computations to worker threads.  <br>
 - Leverage static site generation (SSG) in NextJS to reduce runtime rendering overhead.  <br>
 - Optimize ExpressJS routes with in-memory caching or middleware for faster responses.  <br>
 - Compress assets (e.g., WebP images, minified CSS/JS) and implement lazy loading for resources.<br>
<br>
Key Conventions<br>
- For Electron.js , separate main and renderer processes, enable contextIsolation for security, and use ipcMain/ipcRenderer for communication<br>
- For Express.js , structure routes modularly, validate inputs using middleware, and handle errors globally. Use environment variables securely across all frameworks, and ensure <br>
   proper window management in Electron for a seamless desktop experience.<br>
- Securely handle inter-process communication using ipcMain and ipcRenderer, avoiding direct exposure of sensitive data.  <br>
- Manage application windows effectively using BrowserWindow, and handle lifecycle events like ready-to-show and closed.  <br>
- In PouchDB , use its offline-first capabilities by syncing data with a remote CouchDB instance to ensure seamless offline functionality.  <br>
- Use PouchDB's replication feature to sync local data with the server, ensuring data consistency and availability across devices.<br>
<br>
Follow Next.js docs for Data Fetching, Rendering, and Routing. for Pouchdb you can use these docs https://pouchdb.com/guides/
        </code>

            <!--[if ENDBLOCK]><![endif]-->
        </div>
    </div>
    <!-- End: Keywords -->
</div>
<!-- End: User info and keywords -->

                            <span wire:click="selectTag(29)" class="hover:bg-secondary/80 bg-secondary text-white text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded mr-2 mb-2 cursor-pointer hover:bg-opacity-80 transition-colors duration-300"> TypeScript</span>

        </div>
        <h4 class="text-lg font-semibold mb-2">Replit - TypeScript, React, Express, Shadcn UI, Radix UI,Tailwind, Drizzle, Zod</h4>
        <code class="text-gray-600 group-hover:text-black transition-colors duration-300 rule-content text-sm">
            You are an expert in TypeScript, React, Express, Shadcn UI, Radix UI,Tailwind, Drizzle, Zod, Vite<br>
Code Guidelines<br>
-Concise &amp; Technical: Write clear, technical TypeScript code.<br>
-Functional &amp; Declarative: Use functional components and declarative patterns; avoid classes.<br>
-Modular: Prefer helper functions and modular files.<br>
-Dual Environments: Organize code into client and server folders.<br>
Naming Conventions<br>
-Directories: Lowercase with dashes (e.g., client/auth-wizard, server/api).<br>
-Exports: Use named exports for components and utilities.<br>
-Variables: Use descriptive names (e.g., isLoading, hasError).<br>
TypeScript Usage<br>
-Strict Typing: Use TypeScript everywhere; prefer interfaces for objects.<br>
-Validation: Use drizzle-zod for schema validation.<br>
-Components: Use functional components with proper TS interfaces.<br>
Syntax and Formatting<br>
-Pure Functions: Use function for pure functions.<br>
-Concise Conditionals: Use minimal syntax for simple conditionals.<br>
-Declarative JSX: Write clear, declarative JSX.<br>
UI and Styling<br>
-Libraries: Use Shadcn UI and Radix UI.<br>
-Tailwind CSS: Follow a mobile-first, responsive design.<br>
-Structure: Place UI components in client and separate them from business logic.<br>
Server-Side Considerations<br>
-Express: Organize routes, middleware, and controllers in server.<br>
-Database: Use drizzle-orm with drizzle-zod for type-safe DB interactions.<br>
-Config: Manage environment variables with dotenv and sessions with express-session.<br>
Performance Optimization<br>
-SSR &amp; Splitting: Optimize loads with SSR only when needed.<br>
-React Query: Use tanstack/react-query for client data fetching.<br>
-Dynamic Loading: Wrap non-critical components in Suspense.<br>
-Minimize Client Hooks: Reduce useEffect and similar hooks.
        </code>

    </div>
